    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10037316891786267619"><i>You, dear reader, continue at your own risk. It is not for the faint of heart—no more so than the study of dragons itself. But such study offers rewards beyond compare: to stand in a dragon's presence, even for the briefest of moments—even at the risk of one's life—is a delight that, once experienced, can never be forgotten. . . .</i><br/><br/>All the world, from Scirland to the farthes</span>
  <span id="freeText10037316891786267619" style="display:none"><i>You, dear reader, continue at your own risk. It is not for the faint of heart—no more so than the study of dragons itself. But such study offers rewards beyond compare: to stand in a dragon's presence, even for the briefest of moments—even at the risk of one's life—is a delight that, once experienced, can never be forgotten. . . .</i><br /><br />All the world, from Scirland to the farthest reaches of Eriga, know Isabella, Lady Trent, to be the world's preeminent dragon naturalist. She is the remarkable woman who brought the study of dragons out of the misty shadows of myth and misunderstanding into the clear light of modern science. But before she became the illustrious figure we know today, there was a bookish young woman whose passion for learning, natural history, and, yes, dragons defied the stifling conventions of her day.<br /><br />Here at last, in her own words, is the true story of a pioneering spirit who risked her reputation, her prospects, and her fragile flesh and bone to satisfy her scientific curiosity; of how she sought true love and happiness despite her lamentable eccentricities; and of her thrilling expedition to the perilous mountains of Vystrana, where she made the first of many historic discoveries that would change the world forever.</span>

<div id="review_2399402433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399402433" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7774903635372137797">4.5 stars<blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566770202i/28050513._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>One benefit of being an old woman now, and moreover one who has been called a "national treasure," is that there are very few who can tell me what I may and may not <br/> write.</i>
</blockquote>Ever since she was a child, Isabella was <b>obsessed, <i>absolutely obsessed,</i></b> with dragons. <br/><br/>She would spent long hours <b>curled up with her favorite book,</b> <i>A Natural History of Dragons</i> and for a while, she was indulged by her father...but unfortunately that could not last.<blockquote>
  <i>No gentleman would want a wife covered in scars f</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7774903635372137797" style="display:none">4.5 stars<blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566770202i/28050513._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>One benefit of being an old woman now, and moreover one who has been called a "national treasure," is that there are very few who can tell me what I may and may not <br> write.</i>
</blockquote>Ever since she was a child, Isabella was <b>obsessed, <i>absolutely obsessed,</i></b> with dragons. <br><br>She would spent long hours <b>curled up with her favorite book,</b> <i>A Natural History of Dragons</i> and for a while, she was indulged by her father...but unfortunately that could not last.<blockquote>
  <i>No gentleman would want a wife covered in scars from misadventures with dangerous beasts.</i>
</blockquote>Nowadays she's known as Lady Trent, a world renowned Dragonologist, but she wasn't always quite so well-known...or even well-liked.<br><br>During her early adulthood, all she could think of was<b> finding a husband who would allow </b>her to continue reading. <blockquote>
  <i>"You want me for my library."</i>
</blockquote> And so she marries Jacob, someone who respected her eccentricities, but the newlyweds soon realize life <b>isn't as simple as expected.</b><br><br>A miscarriage and a deep depression results in Isabella realizing that she <b>cannot - <i>will not </i>- ever</b> become the perfect English wife.<blockquote>
  <i>"I don't need luxury, Jacob; I don't need pampering."</i>
</blockquote>And so she secures a position for herself and her husband to participate in an exhibition to far off lands, Vystrana, to study the elusive and mysterious rock-wyrm. <blockquote>
  <i>But as so often happened during this exhibition, nothing went as planned.</i>
</blockquote><b>She is about to discover a whole new world - <i>and change her own forever.<br></i></b><br>Oh my gosh. I<b> LOVED</b> this one. <br><br>Also - I have a confession to make.<br><br>Some girls were obsessed with horses..<b>.I was a dragon girl. </b>Drawing, reading and dreaming - all dragons all the time.<br><br>And this book <b>fulfilled every childhood dream </b>I had. (It was honestly such a blow to realize that dragons didn't exist.)<br><br>This book was so well done. I loved how seriously it took the subject and how firmly grounded the dragon-based world was.<blockquote>
  <i>Sheep eat grass, wolves eat deer, dragons eat everything that doesn't run away fast enough. </i>
</blockquote>The<b> only thing that bugged me</b> was that there was a little less dragons and a little more politics than I expected. <br><br>I did love watching Isabella grow <b>from a timid girl </b>shaped by her times <b>into a strong woman </b>intent on making a life for herself...I just wanted more page time with the dragons.<br><br>Though...that ending was a bit of a shock to the system. Bit of <b>a jump into an icy lake. </b><br><br>In other words, I did NOT appreciate the way the ending wrapped up. <br><br> I honestly cannot imagine where the book is going next.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!<br></span>

    <a title="Christopher Paolini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33610695-christopher-paolini"><img alt="Christopher Paolini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591638018p2/33610695.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2290321808?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher Paolini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher Paolini" href="/user/show/33610695-christopher-paolini">Christopher Paolini</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33610695-christopher-paolini?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2290321808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5945829742607800272"><i>A Natural History of Dragons: A Memoir by Lady Trent</i>, by Marie Brennan, is a superb novel in every regard. It's a classic, first-person adventure full of travel, science, and of course, dragons. The writing is clean, concise, and well-assured. The characters are interesting—especially the main one, Isabella. The plotting is clockwork-tight. And the worldbuilding is a masterpiece of sophisticated evocation. It's clear that Brennan has put an enormous amount of thought and research into her craft.</span>
  <span id="freeText5945829742607800272" style="display:none"><i>A Natural History of Dragons: A Memoir by Lady Trent</i>, by Marie Brennan, is a superb novel in every regard. It's a classic, first-person adventure full of travel, science, and of course, dragons. The writing is clean, concise, and well-assured. The characters are interesting—especially the main one, Isabella. The plotting is clockwork-tight. And the worldbuilding is a masterpiece of sophisticated evocation. It's clear that Brennan has put an enormous amount of thought and research into her craft. From a professional standpoint, I was highly impressed by this book. From a reader's standpoint, I had an absolute blast, and I can't wait to dive into the sequels. Based on this book alone, I place Marie Brennan in the top flight of sci-fi/fantasy authors.</span>

<div id="review_457392382" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457392382" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457392382?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=arc-review">arc-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457392382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6716131130169877251">It turns out, and I wouldn't have discovered this without reading A Natural History of Dragons, that I really like dragons slaying, riding, attacking, hoarding, speaking, snoozing, probably even over-easy ... but to witness them studied for science bored me to death.<br/><br/>I feel really bad about this, because there are some great things about this book, I just couldn't wait for it to be over.<br/><br/>A Natural History of Dragons is a memoir of the life of the famous Lady Trent, who tells about her first intere</span>
  <span id="freeText6716131130169877251" style="display:none">It turns out, and I wouldn't have discovered this without reading A Natural History of Dragons, that I really like dragons slaying, riding, attacking, hoarding, speaking, snoozing, probably even over-easy ... but to witness them studied for science bored me to death.<br><br>I feel really bad about this, because there are some great things about this book, I just couldn't wait for it to be over.<br><br>A Natural History of Dragons is a memoir of the life of the famous Lady Trent, who tells about her first interest in dragons and some of her early experiences with them. <br><br><b>The Good</b><br>Brennan does a great job sticking to character. The Lady Trent, or just Isabella Camherst as she's known throughout the book, is a woman of science and Brennan very convincingly characterizes her as such. She's so brimming with eagerness to study and learn and discover and it's apparent in both the beginning of her life and her characterization later in life that we only get through the actual telling.<br><br>This Victorian era-type place is brought to life with all its sensibilities, especially those that go against a budding young naturalist who is a woman and her constant battle with all those inherent sensibilities. Then she adds dragons to this era! Very cool. Especially since they're all over, from the tiny sparklings that are considered to be insects by many to much larger ones.<br><br>And then there's the beautiful artwork by Todd Lockwood. Not only do we get this gorgeous cover, but there are dragons (among other things) depicted throughout the book that are just as captivating.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397863i/768134._SX540_.jpg" width="350" height="275" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I realize the book cover's in the upper left, but this bears repeating!)<br><br><b>The Bad</b><br>The problem is that with the over-intrusion of the narrator, Lady Trent, and possibly with the addition of the aristocracy's confidence in their own imperviousness, there really isn't a lot of suspense. Possibly at the very end at one single moment, but that's it. We already know she's fine, she's telling the story and interjecting points about how young and naive she used to be. Now, you can say this about most first-person narratives, but this was even more obvious.<br><br>The characters are just not relatable to me. I mentioned above that Brennan nailed the era, but these are high class people that can't even go anywhere without a servant of some sort. I just couldn't love them and I'll take responsibility for this - I know plenty of people love it, but it did not work for me.<br><br>It took me a while to figure this out, but it sounds like we're going to get through her whole life in this one book, when really it's only the first couple experiences. Therefore, it seemed to drag on (dragon, get it) this one event. The Lady Trent alludes to many experiences, especially early on, and it sounds like those are all going to happen in this book, but it took me till about 50% in to figure out that it was mainly focused on this one event and that was it. This also could have just been my lack of awareness about sequels because I thought this was a stand-alone book.<br><br>In the end, I really do think the problems were mostly just me. A Natural History of Dragons is a well-executed story that I found was just not for me.<br><br>2 out of 5 Stars (Just Okay)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6716131130169877251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1364461930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364461930" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364461930?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Robin Hobb fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364461930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11425644106472035064">I like books about people who like books. Perhaps it’s because it immediately allows me to sympathise with the protagonist as a bond of kinship is created. Or perhaps it’s because reading about books is a double winner. Well, either way it creates a novel that is easy to relate to and easy to become engrossed in. <br/><br/><b> A well created discipline </b><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1439646865p8/1222823.jpg' width='400' height='533' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This is not a standard novel; it is in the form of a memoir of sorts. Lady Trent is writing, what is essentially, her life story. She is now an aged and accr</span>
  <span id="freeText11425644106472035064" style="display:none">I like books about people who like books. Perhaps it’s because it immediately allows me to sympathise with the protagonist as a bond of kinship is created. Or perhaps it’s because reading about books is a double winner. Well, either way it creates a novel that is easy to relate to and easy to become engrossed in. <br><br><b> A well created discipline </b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1439646865p8/1222823.jpg" width="400" height="533" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is not a standard novel; it is in the form of a memoir of sorts. Lady Trent is writing, what is essentially, her life story. She is now an aged and accredited dragon naturalist without equal; it took her years to become this successful; thus, she narrates the story of how she struggled to become recognised and taken with a degree of seriousness. It began when she stumbled on a book about dragons in her father’s library. She is a woman, and considered a part of the nobility because she is the daughter of a knight. Consequently, society has two reasons to consider her choice of profession inappropriate. As true as that may be to these chracters, it would never stop her perusing her interest. <br><br><i>"Be warned, then: the collected volumes of this series will contain frozen mountains, foetid swamps, hostile foreigners, hostile fellow countrymen, the occasional hostile family member, bad decisions, misadventures in orienteering, diseases of an unromantic sort, and a plenitude of mud."</i><br><br>This, for me, made the story quite strong. She is looking back on the timidity of her youth with a voice of frankness and wisdom. She has overcome her trials and has been recognised academically. She is a strong woman; she can now see the absurdity of the gender restrictions she was forced to endure; she has developed the confidence to question the ridiculousness of it, and at the same time has captured the essence of her naïve young self. The effect of this was a memoir that felt real; it felt like I’d picked this up from someone’s shelf in a fantasy universe. <br><br><b> Eventually it became a little dry </b><br><br>The older narrator is a developed naturalist; she has gone on to achieve progress in her discipline. This is all well and good, but eventually I began to grow a little tired of her narrative. I felt because of the memoir style of the writing some of the chapters didn’t link together particularly well. This didn’t have the flow of a normal novel, and at times I had to glance back at pervious chapters to remind myself of what had happened. In addition to this, at times it felt like she was repeating herself, and her justification for killing a dragon was also plain weak. In it she suggested the hypocrisy of dragon rights activists; they argue that hunting dragons is wrong but it’s ok to kill other creatures in the same way. That’s true: it is hypocrisy. But, that doesn’t justify her argument. She basically says because other people do it, it is then ok for her to do the same. This part of the memoir should have been left out in my opinion because it made Lady Trent look like an idiot, which she is most definitely is not. <br><br>Overall, I think this book was a really good idea but the execution of it was lacking. I will be avoiding the rest in the serious because, no doubt, I will find them growing tedious on me. I would, however, recommend this to fans of Robin Hobb because Lady Trent reminded me of the dragon obsessed lady in the rain wild chronicles. I’m sure this is merely coincidence, but if you liked that character Lady Trent is very much the same.<br><br><b> A natural three stars </b><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11425644106472035064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sanaa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5944522-sanaa"><img alt="Sanaa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562015335p2/5944522.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sanaa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sanaa" href="/user/show/5944522-sanaa">Sanaa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765375070" href="/book/show/17910164-a-natural-history-of-dragons">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5944522-sanaa?shelf=favorites-2015">favorites-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5944522-sanaa?shelf=book-collection">book-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5944522-sanaa?shelf=series-completed">series-completed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer765071719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14438593113396700772">[5 Stars] I loved this book. I knew I loved this book after reading only two pages of it. I'm finding it difficult to say anything right now because I loved it that much. This series may even become an all time favorite if each book is as good or better than this one.<br/><br/>Though this book is called <i>A Natural History of Dragons</i> it is really more about Lady Trent and how she initially became interested in dragons and also her experience on her first dragon studying expedition. This book also deals with</span>
  <span id="freeText14438593113396700772" style="display:none">[5 Stars] I loved this book. I knew I loved this book after reading only two pages of it. I'm finding it difficult to say anything right now because I loved it that much. This series may even become an all time favorite if each book is as good or better than this one.<br /><br />Though this book is called <i>A Natural History of Dragons</i> it is really more about Lady Trent and how she initially became interested in dragons and also her experience on her first dragon studying expedition. This book also deals with the struggles Lady Trent has to deal with because she is a female in a society that looks down on particularly headstrong women. I loved how this almost Victorian England setting interacts with the fantasy/scientific world of dragons and Lady Trent's almost <i>coming of age</i> story.<br /><br />I loved the way this book was written: the humor, the spunk, the romance, the science, everything. If there was a book that appealed specifically to my taste this would be the one. Lady Trent is literally my kind of lady. Oh, and did I mentioned there are gorgeous illustrations throughout?! The one thing I will say that is disappointing is the lack of development for the side characters. They often felt bland.<br /><br />Overall, if you love fantasy of manners, smart spunky female protagonists, slower fantasy books without many dragons, and brilliant writing this one is definitely for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14438593113396700772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2871594768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2871594768" />
    <a title="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84916113-somebunny-reads-phoenix"><img alt="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600928258p2/84916113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2871594768?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" class="user" itemprop="url" name="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" href="/user/show/84916113-somebunny-reads-phoenix">¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84916113-somebunny-reads-phoenix?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84916113-somebunny-reads-phoenix?shelf=2019-favorites">2019-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871594768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7646380131133865977"><i>“The dragon within my heart stirred, shifting her wings, as if remembering they could be used to fly.”</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563173329i/27829650._SX540_.png' alt='dragons-by-todd-lockwood' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Before starting this book I've been warned by many people: "A Natural History of dragons is <i>not</i> a book about dragons"; which is, on one hand, correct. This fictional memoir follows the life and adventures of Lady Isabella Trent, a woman who, despite her gender and upbringing, became the most influential expert on dragons of her time. In truth, this book focuses so much on her life and her recall</span>
  <span id="freeText7646380131133865977" style="display:none"><i>“The dragon within my heart stirred, shifting her wings, as if remembering they could be used to fly.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563173329i/27829650._SX540_.png" alt="dragons-by-todd-lockwood" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Before starting this book I've been warned by many people: "A Natural History of dragons is <i>not</i> a book about dragons"; which is, on one hand, correct. This fictional memoir follows the life and adventures of Lady Isabella Trent, a woman who, despite her gender and upbringing, became the most influential expert on dragons of her time. In truth, this book focuses so much on her life and her recalling of the events that the presence of dragons as the subject of her studies, appears, on one hand, to be marginal. On the other hand, even if it was true that Lady Trent's expeditions could have been about any other wild animal, or even just explorations of the wilderness, the fact that the animal in question is a <i>dragon</i>, makes it 200% cooler. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563173329i/27829651.jpg" alt="9780765331960-il-2" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Indeed, my favourite feature in this book was the contrast between the old-fashioned, predictable character of Lady Trent (a strong, revolutionary woman of her time who challenges gender stereotypes with the ambition to become a scholar) and the subject of her studies. It felt like seeing Jane Eyre riding unicorns! I adored the choice of the author in creating this element of absurd, and I appreciated the fact that she didn't try to make Lady Trent different from exactly how you would imagine a character like herself in those situations. She is, of course, predictable and the other characters are as well; the story is predictable too, in a way; but, I mean, we're talking about <i>dragons</i>! I thought just the idea of this book was very clever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563173329i/27829649.jpg" alt="history-dragons3" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally, the book itself is very entertaining, and I was very involved with the plot. Not so much with the characters, for whom I didn't really feel much affection... The cold, scientific way of writing of the fictional author might have been the main reason for that, but also a general coldness surrounding human relationships in those years. Overall, I found this book very interesting and I would love to go on with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7646380131133865977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3481623052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3481623052" />
    <a title="Lisann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104031480-lisann"><img alt="Lisann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592343074p2/104031480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3481623052?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisann" href="/user/show/104031480-lisann">Lisann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765375070" href="/book/show/17910164-a-natural-history-of-dragons">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104031480-lisann?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3481623052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3316964781726433166"><blockquote>
  <i>“The dragon within my heart stirred, shifting her wings, as if remembering they could be used to fly.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>A Natural History of Dragons is not a classic fantasy story. It reads more like a <b>historical fiction novel in which dragons are a rare animal species</b>. They have yet to be explored and that's exactly what our protagonist wants. The only problem is her own gender! <b>Isabella is a woman and society doesn't even allow her to wear pants, so how could she become a scientist?</b><br/><br/>In this series she tells </span>
  <span id="freeText3316964781726433166" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“The dragon within my heart stirred, shifting her wings, as if remembering they could be used to fly.”</i>
</blockquote><br>A Natural History of Dragons is not a classic fantasy story. It reads more like a <b>historical fiction novel in which dragons are a rare animal species</b>. They have yet to be explored and that's exactly what our protagonist wants. The only problem is her own gender! <b>Isabella is a woman and society doesn't even allow her to wear pants, so how could she become a scientist?</b><br><br>In this series she tells <b>how exactly she became a <u>renowned dragon naturalist</u></b>. The first book focuses on the beginning of her career. As a result, the <b>role of the woman</b> is often depicted here and how difficult it is for Isabella to hide her passion for the anatomy and behaviour of dragons. I found this part very difficult to read in the long run because I still get upset about how bad it must have been back then. See? <b>Historical fiction!</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Be warned, then: the collected volumes of this series will contain frozen mountains, foetid swamps, hostile foreigners, hostile fellow countrymen, the occasional hostile family member, bad decisions, misadventures in orienteering, diseases of an unromantic sort, and a plenitude of mud.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Unfortunately I expected a bit more from this story. <b>As the book progresses, the focus is more on the problems with villagers and their superstitions</b>. There are problems that seem to be of supernatural origin, but I have to disappoint you here. As mentioned at the beginning, the fantasy part of this book is limited to the existence of dragons. <b> Here you won't find any magic, mythical creatures</b> or other things that would be different from our real world. Now one could of course hope that there is at least a bunch of <b>interactions with dragons</b>, but most take place when they're already dead and dissected to explore their anatomy.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596894599i/29934954.png" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all it was a nice story for in between, but I probably won't continue the series, because the reviews of the second book confirmed my opinion and<b> the focus of the book shifts even further away from the dragons and more to political topics.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3316964781726433166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3154266050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3154266050" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3154266050?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3154266050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6006371619031060352">I think I'm in love with this book. No... I know it. :)<br/><br/>I don't know what I expected, but it wasn't a call-back to the early days of science when the practitioners called themselves Naturalists, being well-funded amateurs and Lords (Or Ladies!) striking out into the wide world for the simple pleasure of learning, discovery, and adventure.<br/><br/>Maybe I should have expected that. But then, maybe I shouldn't have expected it to be charming, totally delightful, emotionally rewarding, smart, and witty... bu</span>
  <span id="freeText6006371619031060352" style="display:none">I think I'm in love with this book. No... I know it. :)<br /><br />I don't know what I expected, but it wasn't a call-back to the early days of science when the practitioners called themselves Naturalists, being well-funded amateurs and Lords (Or Ladies!) striking out into the wide world for the simple pleasure of learning, discovery, and adventure.<br /><br />Maybe I should have expected that. But then, maybe I shouldn't have expected it to be charming, totally delightful, emotionally rewarding, smart, and witty... but then, I did get that, too.<br /><br />But the real kicker? I was caught and dipped in vinegar the very moment that we began wondering whether dragons had wishbones. The total love of books, the frustration that women with talent and drive always experience when they're told they're not allowed in certain fields, and the utter DEMAND one puts on oneself to succeed at all costs... well, THIS is what preserved me.<br /><br />Great observations, charmingly told, this is almost like Indiana Jones with Dragons as written by a wonderfully quirky woman with a sharp eye. I can't recommend this enough.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3197553472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3197553472" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3197553472?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781783292394" href="/book/show/21167966-a-natural-history-of-dragons">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3197553472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17045135970675666787">By right, I should have loved and adored this. A regency-style world, very Austen-y, with a strong female lead and with the added spice of DRAGONS! Sadly, I'm not really all that charmed.<br/><br/>We have here the first volume in the "auto-biography" of Lady Trent, a scholar of dragons. In this first volume, we follow her childhood and teenage years until she gets married and a bit further. <br/>She's always been a bit of a tomboy and a bookworm, to say nothing of her love for natural history. After finding a </span>
  <span id="freeText17045135970675666787" style="display:none">By right, I should have loved and adored this. A regency-style world, very Austen-y, with a strong female lead and with the added spice of DRAGONS! Sadly, I'm not really all that charmed.<br /><br />We have here the first volume in the "auto-biography" of Lady Trent, a scholar of dragons. In this first volume, we follow her childhood and teenage years until she gets married and a bit further. <br />She's always been a bit of a tomboy and a bookworm, to say nothing of her love for natural history. After finding a particular tome in her father's library, she loves nothing more than dragons (which I can relate to). For in this world, they aren't mythical creatures but wild animals!<br />One day, she meets the perfect husband, Jacob, gets married and even manages to talk him into taking her on an expedition (highly unusual for a woman back then).<br />Heartbreak and elation follow in equal measure as we accompany Lady Trent on her way to scholarly fame.<br /><br />The idea of a book about the natural history of dragons fascinated me. I have always loved reading about naturalists such as Charles Darwin, Alexander von Humboldt and others and how they started or at least heavily influenced the scientific process culminating in what we know and do today, so the idea of a (fictional) female naturalist not giving a damn about convention and travelling the globe to study THE fantastical creatures invented by human minds, sounded wonderful.<br /><br />Sadly, while the writing isn't bad and while the characters aren't terrible (though also far from lively and nuanced) and while the events are interesting enough, I was never sucked in the way I had anticipated/hoped and I just can't imagine reading 4 more books like this (albeit about other dragon species / exploits).<br />Makes me want to cry, really, but here we are. I am wondering if I'm just in a strange mood and if that might have influenced (marred) my enjoyment of this tale or if it was the fact that there were hardly any dragons here on top of my other complaints. Since I'm not entirely sure, I'm giving this 2.5 stars but rounding up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17045135970675666787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1582470908" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582470908" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3300744-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271108982p2/3300744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582470908?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/3300744-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22387085-a-natural-history-of-dragons">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3300744-sam?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3300744-sam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582470908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16520208715444042816">It took me a long time to pick this up. I always loved the cover, but something about it kept me from thinking it was going to be up my alley. I was wrong and I’m glad I finally decided to give this one a chance. It probably turned into a 3.5 star book for me but I’m rounding up.<br/><br/>It’s definitely a different sort of book – it’s got a very Victorian feel. I guess this should be obvious given that’s the sort of setting the author is trying for, but sometimes that feels like a barrier from me connect</span>
  <span id="freeText16520208715444042816" style="display:none">It took me a long time to pick this up. I always loved the cover, but something about it kept me from thinking it was going to be up my alley. I was wrong and I’m glad I finally decided to give this one a chance. It probably turned into a 3.5 star book for me but I’m rounding up.<br /><br />It’s definitely a different sort of book – it’s got a very Victorian feel. I guess this should be obvious given that’s the sort of setting the author is trying for, but sometimes that feels like a barrier from me connecting fully to the book. It’s almost as if the book begins to feel as prim and proper as the characters strive to be and that’s definitely not my personality. Plus this is less about dragons than I really thought it was going to be. Dragons are involved, but the book and the plot seem to swirl around them rather than getting involved too directly. I guess it’s just at odds with most fantasy books where the dragons can talk, or at the very least, have a larger than life presence. Not to say that I didn’t like this take on them, it’s just different from what I’ve come to known of dragons. <br /> <br />Lady Trent is a fun protagonist. She had a bit of the cliché “Victorian girl who’s not quite like the others” aka she’s smart, plucky, and wants to be a badass in a man’s world. It’s not a bad cliché but just sort of obvious. I did like that she makes mistakes and acknowledges them. The rest of the characters are a bit flat for me. It’ll be interesting if they re-appear in sequels. Hopefully if they do some depth gets added as I don’t really think any of them added much to the story.<br /><br />The plot does meander a bit. It’s a bit of an origin story before we get anywhere near what seems to be the core of this book and the formula for the books going forward. It’s not terrible but a bit much of the plucky girl turns plucky woman which we’ve all read before. The core of the book has a bit of a mystery thrown in. It felt a tad underdone and I think just too much time was spent on the origin story to have time to fully dive into a mystery. But the book is pretty short so I think it was well-done for the amount of pages given to it.<br /><br />All-in-all I’d recommend this book. I’m definitely going to continue on in the series. It’s fun and quite easy to read. Hopefully they get even better.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16520208715444042816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1623471586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623471586" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623471586?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623471586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9762340826511491941">Genuinely I loved this. I picked this up at long last at what I felt was the perfect time. not only had two of my great friends been recently discussing it and saying how much they enjoyed it (Paul and Elizabeth) but they also mentioned the focus on anatomy and science and drawing of Dragons. I've owned this book for literally years now, and I felt like it was about time I got to reading it. I'm so glad that the time I chose to start it was also the time when I was involved in drawing Dinosaur a</span>
  <span id="freeText9762340826511491941" style="display:none">Genuinely I loved this. I picked this up at long last at what I felt was the perfect time. not only had two of my great friends been recently discussing it and saying how much they enjoyed it (Paul and Elizabeth) but they also mentioned the focus on anatomy and science and drawing of Dragons. I've owned this book for literally years now, and I felt like it was about time I got to reading it. I'm so glad that the time I chose to start it was also the time when I was involved in drawing Dinosaur anatomy for University, as Dinos and Dragons are not too far removed and the blend of book and project helped me to fully immerse myself within this world :)<br /><br />This story follows the early life of Lady Trent who we know as Isabella. She's a young lady with a dangerous passion: Dragons. In this world Dragons are rare, but not uncommon in some areas of the world. Isabella has always had a passion for the majestic beasts, and she's made a habit of 'borrowing' books on the subject from her father and sneaking in to see the beasts if ever an opportunity arises. We follow, in Lady Trent's own words, her childhood and early adult life including her first excursion to discover more about the creatures and also get involved in the mysteries of life abroad. The adventure is real and raw, and filled with dangers no-one foresaw, but she and her friends are resourceful.<br /><br />The pacing and plotting of this book are fantastic allowing the reader to follow easily and yet be drawn in. The very British sensibilities make this a wonderfully amusing read at times too, and seeing Lady Trent face the difficulties of being a woman in a man's world really worked. Isabella is lucky enough to be surrounded by men who are more free with her than most would be, and so she enjoys things rather unladylike. I loved seeing the adventurous explorer and researcher within the prim and proper facade!<br /><br />This book made me laugh and smile, chuckle and roll my eyes and even get a little bit emotional too. I would recommend this to fans of Gail Carriger's books as I think that they have a similar feel, even if it's rather more focused on Dragons than Vamps/Werewolves. A splendid read, 5*s, and I already have book #2 waiting for me to dive into it :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9762340826511491941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3070156475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3070156475" />
    <a title="Allison Hurd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd"><img alt="Allison Hurd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530670583p2/14495279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3070156475?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Hurd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Hurd" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd">Allison Hurd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-bookshelf">sff-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-2019-challenge">sff-2019-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fem-author">fem-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3070156475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6635891129315855415">This was quite enjoyable. Part Regency memoir, part travelogue, part adventure story, part cozy mystery, it was just pleasant.<br/><br/><b>CONTENT WARNINGS</b>: (just a list of topics) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[dissection, miscarriage, loss of loved ones, intentional and casual racism, misogyny  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><u>Things to love:</u><br/><br/>-<b>The combination of archetypes</b>. If you like flintlock fantasy AND Regency AND mysteries AND...all the rest, this is a must-read. I didn't think they'd all manage to blend as well as they did and I was </span>
  <span id="freeText6635891129315855415" style="display:none">This was quite enjoyable. Part Regency memoir, part travelogue, part adventure story, part cozy mystery, it was just pleasant.<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNINGS</b>: (just a list of topics) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dissection, miscarriage, loss of loved ones, intentional and casual racism, misogyny  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Things to love:</u><br /><br />-<b>The combination of archetypes</b>. If you like flintlock fantasy AND Regency AND mysteries AND...all the rest, this is a must-read. I didn't think they'd all manage to blend as well as they did and I was quite impressed.<br /><br />-<b>Isabella.</b> Plucky, flawed but earnest, and the walking embodiment of "I do what I want." Sometimes to a fault.<br /><br />-<b>The relationships</b>. The parents, lovers, friends, colleagues, siblings...all of them felt so charming.<br /><br />-<b>The conceit</b>. An older woman who broke barriers and is now doing her tell all on her career and life?? But that life is about being like the Jane Goodall meets Miss Phrynne Fisher of women, and the gorillas are instead dragons????? I keep coming back to the mash up! Someone mixed this just for me, I think.<br /><br />-<b>The tone</b>. I really liked just putting this on and letting it lull me to sleep. Not because it was boring, but because it was just so pleasant, both in content and narration, that I could listen to it even when I was mentally and physically exhausted and be soothed. <br /><br />-<b>The ultimate ending</b>. I liked that things were wrapped up, but not neatly, and that there's the promise of more without it feeling like a cliffhanger. Well done.<br /><br /><u>Things that hampered my reading:</u><br /><br />-<b>The casual racism</b>. Look there are stereotypes in here, there's no avoiding it. They're secondary world, but they're <i>very clearly</i> based on certain cultures in our world and it was a bit weird that we needed that, given that it wasn't really our world, and that Isabella calls out her impolitic moments but not about these impressions she formed. So I'm left to believe the author didn't see an issue. This may have been compounded by the audio narrator's voice selection which was...pronounced. She's talented but it didn't help sand the rough edges off the prose.<br /><br />-<b>The mystery felt a bit tacked on</b>. I don't even know how you go about combining all the things that got combined, and I think this was a great effort, but the seams show a bit. I got Scooby Doo flashes.<br /><br />-<b>Some nonsensical bits</b>. Every time this woman wakes up without her husband staring at her full in the face, she's doing stupid shit. You'd think after the third or fourth time she manages to get kidnapped or haunted or whatever, she'd say to herself "you know what? Let me just wake Jacob, I shouldn't go alone as I always seem to stumble into cults or whatever." Same with a few other characters' responses. <br /><br />-<b>The end of the study</b>. It just bummed me out when I didn't want to be bummed, I wanted to feel victorious.<br /><br />Not perfect, but perfectly delightful. Absolutely adding this to my list of "more or less feel good as long as you squint" books. I will be continuing the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6635891129315855415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_773928175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773928175" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/773928175?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=sword-and-laser">sword-and-laser</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer773928175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13572865056480208402"><b>Executive Summary:</b> The book has surprisingly few dragons in it for being in the title of the book. It's still a decent book, but I found myself underwhelmed by the end of it.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I was hesitant to read this book when it was announced as the December pick for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sword & Laser</a>. I like dragons, but the concept of this book made me apprehensive.<br/><br/>I ended up really enjoying the start of this book though. It really appealed to my inner scientist that wants to categorize things and understand how </span>
  <span id="freeText13572865056480208402" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> The book has surprisingly few dragons in it for being in the title of the book. It's still a decent book, but I found myself underwhelmed by the end of it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I was hesitant to read this book when it was announced as the December pick for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword &amp; Laser</a>. I like dragons, but the concept of this book made me apprehensive.<br /><br />I ended up really enjoying the start of this book though. It really appealed to my inner scientist that wants to categorize things and understand how they work.<br /><br />The main character of Lady Trent is well written. You can tell the difference of her as a girl/young woman and the elderly "I don't give a damn" renowned scholar. The humor while not abundant was pretty good.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I was expecting a series of stories about her time as a dragon naturalist exactly, but I wasn't expecting so much of her time courting her husband and her early life struggling with her interests in Natural History and science in a society where it's not proper for woman to do so.<br /><br />I expected a lot more dragons stuff. Even if it was time spent analzing and discovering things about dragons. There was certainly some of that, but it was more of a backdrop to the story of Lady Trent's early life.<br /><br />This feels like the first book in a series, and maybe later stories will include a lot more about her life as a Dragon Naturalist. This just felt like too much setup for me.<br /><br />It ends in a decent enough place and is well written, but it just wasn't really for me. At this point I don't plan on continuing the series (if it does indeed turn into one), but I imagine people who really enjoy Lady Trent, might thoroughly enjoy this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13572865056480208402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1950934736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1950934736" />
    <a title="Beatriz Cunha Tavares ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56600798-beatriz-cunha-tavares"><img alt="Beatriz Cunha Tavares ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502803480p2/56600798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1950934736?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatriz Cunha Tavares ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatriz Cunha Tavares ☾" href="/user/show/56600798-beatriz-cunha-tavares">Beatriz Cunha Tavares ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1950934736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4349510028311476781"><b>4.75*</b><br/><br/>Lovely book, a total surprise. It was an easy read that really grabed my attention and was hard to put down. <br/><br/>I loved the world, that was very "normal", with normal animals and a normal society ressembling the 19th century. Sometimes it felt almost like I was reading a goood historical fiction... with dragons! I don't usually read a lot of books about dragons, but in this one they were nicely imagined and described and fit very well in the story. <br/>The prose was beautifully written and had rea</span>
  <span id="freeText4349510028311476781" style="display:none"><b>4.75*</b><br /><br />Lovely book, a total surprise. It was an easy read that really grabed my attention and was hard to put down. <br /><br />I loved the world, that was very "normal", with normal animals and a normal society ressembling the 19th century. Sometimes it felt almost like I was reading a goood historical fiction... with dragons! I don't usually read a lot of books about dragons, but in this one they were nicely imagined and described and fit very well in the story. <br />The prose was beautifully written and had really nice nature descriptions, like the forests or the night sky. Once again, also loved the 1st person, one POV, since I've been reading too much multiple POV's lately. <br />The main characters personality, which most of the time felt "misplaced", was a really strong part of the story to me - she doesn't let society's chains keep her from doing what she loves to do, and ends up becoming a successful science woman. I think that's a very important message. Also loved the fact that her brothers, father and then her husband were supportive of her "strange" hobbies and dreams, unlike her mother - society's prejudices towards women sometimes come from women themselves, and not always from men. <br /><br />However, I guess I don't give this book a full 5* for two reasons:<br />- I wish there was a little more depth and development to some of the other characters - I understand this is a 1st person POV, so Isabella knows how she feels but doesn't know how others feel. Still, I think her character was very well developed while the other fell a little too flat sometimes;<br />- The way the dragons (and other wild life) was sometimes killed (almost casualy as if it were nothing) bugged me a little, and I have to admit that's a bit of a down side to me. <br /><br />But overall it was a very good book that i really enjoyed reading. Would definitely recomend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4349510028311476781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1922537566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922537566" />
    <a title="Wol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5973651-wol"><img alt="Wol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518815855p2/5973651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922537566?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wol" href="/user/show/5973651-wol">Wol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765375070" href="/book/show/17910164-a-natural-history-of-dragons">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Robin Hobb fans, Jane Austen fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973651-wol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973651-wol?shelf=r-fantasy-bingo-2017">r-fantasy-bingo-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922537566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1505446348876705610">I'll preface this review with something that I feel it's important to know.<br/><br/>This book is not for everyone. It's really, *really* not for everyone. If you read Fantasy for lots of action, wish fulfillment, badass overpowered characters, action scenes, battles, intricate plot and heavy world building, run. Run far, run fast, and don't look back. <i>It's not for you, Jen.</i><br/><br/>If you enjoy a good character piece, if you have an interest in science and natural history, if you enjoy classical literature in the</span>
  <span id="freeText1505446348876705610" style="display:none">I'll preface this review with something that I feel it's important to know.<br /><br />This book is not for everyone. It's really, *really* not for everyone. If you read Fantasy for lots of action, wish fulfillment, badass overpowered characters, action scenes, battles, intricate plot and heavy world building, run. Run far, run fast, and don't look back. <i>It's not for you, Jen.</i><br /><br />If you enjoy a good character piece, if you have an interest in science and natural history, if you enjoy classical literature in the vein of Jane Austen and the Brontës, if David Attenborough is listed amongst your personal heroes, if you want something light and gentle and a bit whimsical, or if you just feel like trying something a little <i>different</i>, you're in the right place. <br /><br />In A Natural History of Dragons, a Victorian lady defies the rules of society and heads off into the wilds on an expedition to study dragons. The Victorian "voice" is well written and convincing, the main character flawed but likeable, and the adventure eventually leads to an interesting mystery/conspiracy. It's written like an old timey adventure, something you might expect from the likes of Sir Arthur Conan Doyle or Rudyard Kipling. And it works. I have knocked off one star because it did get a little bit dry in places and the plot meandered just a touch too often, but there's a great deal to enjoy here and honestly, well done for doing something different. In a sea of Drizzts and Durzo Blints, here stands Lady Trent. Strong, (mostly) dignified, and very much her own person. Good for her. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1505446348876705610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
